colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<i>As of 20 June 2018</i></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Scotland national cricket team</b> represents the country of <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_Scotland" title="Cricket in Scotland">Scotland</a>. They play their home matches at <a href="/wiki/The_Grange_Club" title="The Grange Club">The Grange, Edinburgh</a>.\n</p><p>Scotland became associate members of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC) in 1994<sup id="cite_ref-ScoCA_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScoCA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> after severing links with the <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England cricket team</a> two years earlier. Since then, they have played in three <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cups</a> (1999, 2007 and 2015) and three <a href="/wiki/ICC_World_Twenty20" title="ICC World Twenty20">ICC World Twenty20</a> tournaments (2007, 2009 and 2016). However, their first win in either of these events did not come until they beat <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_national_cricket_team" title="Hong Kong national cricket team">Hong Kong</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2016 ICC World Twenty20">2016 World Twenty20</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Scottish cricket team is governed by <a href="/wiki/Cricket_Scotland" title="Cricket Scotland">Cricket Scotland</a>.\n</p><p>Scotland have also played in every <a href="/wiki/ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="ICC Intercontinental Cup">ICC Intercontinental Cup</a> tournament, winning the inaugural edition in <a href="/wiki/2004_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2004 ICC Intercontinental Cup">2004</a>. Between 2010 and 2013, the team competed in the <a href="/wiki/ECB_40" title="ECB 40">ECB 40</a> as the <b>Scottish Saltires</b>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kyle_Coetzer" title="Kyle Coetzer">Kyle Coetzer</a> became captain of the side in November 2016 after <a href="/wiki/Preston_Mommsen" title="Preston Mommsen">Preston Mommsen</a> who had captained the side since September 2014 stepped down.  The coach is New Zealander <a href="/wiki/Grant_Bradburn" title="Grant Bradburn">Grant Bradburn</a>, who took on the role in April 2014.\n</p><p>In April 2018, the ICC decided to grant full <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 International</a> (T20I) status to all its members. Therefore, all <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> matches played between Scotland and other <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">ICC members</a> after 1 January 2019 will be a full T20I.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Before_ICC_membership"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Before ICC tournaments</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Personnel"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Personnel</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Playing_staff"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Playing staff</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Coaching_staff"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Coaching staff</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Coaches"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_ICC_membership">Before ICC membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Before ICC membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first recorded cricket match in Scotland took place in <a href="/wiki/Alloa" title="Alloa">Alloa</a> in 1785.<sup id="cite_ref-Hist_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hist-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It would be another eighty years, however, before Scotland played their first full match, against <a href="/wiki/Surrey_County_Cricket_Club" title="Surrey County Cricket Club">Surrey</a> in 1865, which they won by 172 runs.\n</p><p>The first Scottish Cricket Union was formed in 1879, and the national team beat <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a> by 7 wickets three years later. The cricket union became defunct in 1883, and Grange Cricket Club took over the administration of the game until 1909. The first match against <a href="/wiki/Ireland_cricket_team" title="Ireland cricket team">Ireland</a> took place in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> in 1888, with Ireland winning. They also played South Africa, West Indies, an all-Indian team, and New Zealand before the start of World War II.\n</p><p>1948 saw Australia visit Scotland for two games at the end of their tour of England. These games, both of which were won by the Australians, were to be the last international games for <a href="/wiki/Don_Bradman" title="Don Bradman">Don Bradman</a>. The Don signed off in typical style, making a fine unbeaten 123 in the innings victory.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_c_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_c-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland first competed in English domestic cricket in 1980, when they competed in the <a href="/wiki/Benson_%26_Hedges_Cup" title="Benson &amp; Hedges Cup">Benson &amp; Hedges Cup</a> for the first time. Three years later they took part in the NatWest Trophy. Their first Benson &amp; Hedges win came against <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Lancashire County Cricket Club">Lancashire</a> in 1986.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_cricketers">Scottish cricketers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Scottish cricketers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The most famous cricketers to have come from Scotland are probably the former <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="English cricket team">England</a> captain, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Denness" title="Mike Denness">Mike Denness</a>, Warwickshire all-rounder <a href="/wiki/Dougie_Brown" title="Dougie Brown">Dougie Brown</a>, and former England Test player <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Hamilton_(cricketer)" title="Gavin Hamilton (cricketer)">Gavin Hamilton</a>. Another great Scottish cricketer was B.R. (Lager) Hardie, who was a major contributor to the successful Essex side of the 1970s and 1980s. Possibly one of the best spinners and certainly a respected journalist was the aptly named <a href="/wiki/Ian_Peebles" title="Ian Peebles">Ian Peebles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> who was one of the cricketers of the year in 1931 alongside Don Bradman.\n</p><p>The most infamous cricketer, a man who was vilified in Australia, was a Scot, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Jardine" title="Douglas Jardine">Douglas Jardine</a>, father to and inventor of "Body Theory", which is well documented under "<a href="/wiki/Bodyline" title="Bodyline">Bodyline</a>". Jardine was born in British India, and died in Switzerland, spending most of his life in England. However, his parents were Scottish. He asked for his ashes to be scattered in Scotland and gave his own children Scottish names.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICC_membership">ICC membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: ICC membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1992 Scotland severed their ties with the <a href="/wiki/Test_and_County_Cricket_Board" title="Test and County Cricket Board">Test and County Cricket Board</a> (TCCB) and England, and gained <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members#Associate_members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">associate membership of the ICC</a> in their own right in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-ScoCA_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScoCA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> They competed in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_World_Cup_Qualifier" title="ICC World Cup Qualifier">ICC Trophy</a> for the first time in <a href="/wiki/1997_ICC_Trophy" title="1997 ICC Trophy">1997</a>, finishing third and qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/1999_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1999 Cricket World Cup">1999 World Cup</a>, where they lost all their games.<sup id="cite_ref-WC99_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WC99-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2001_ICC_Trophy" title="2001 ICC Trophy">2001 ICC Trophy</a> saw them finish 4th, losing a play-off game to <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_cricket_team" title="Canada national cricket team">Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ICCT01_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICCT01-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> but they won the <a href="/wiki/2005_ICC_Trophy" title="2005 ICC Trophy">2005 tournament</a>, beating long-time rivals Ireland in the final. 2004 saw Scotland first confirm themselves as one of the leading associate nations by winning the inaugural <a href="/wiki/ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="ICC Intercontinental Cup">Intercontinental Cup</a>. However, they did not progress beyond the first round in the 2005 tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-ICCup05_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICCup05-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006">2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg/250px-Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2f/Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg/375px-Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2f/Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="267" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_watson_india_odi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scotland\'s <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Watson_(cricketer)" title="Ryan Watson (cricketer)">Ryan Watson</a> plays through backward point for a boundary against India at Glasgow\'s <a href="/wiki/Citylets_Titwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Citylets Titwood">Titwood</a> ground, 16 August 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>March 2006 saw Scotland embark on a pre-season tour to <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>. They performed with some credit, although they only won one of their 6 games, against a Barbados XI.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_d_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_d-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> They owed much of their success to Dougie Brown, who re-qualified to represent Scotland internationally in 2004. They competed in the <a href="/wiki/Friends_Provident_Trophy" title="Friends Provident Trophy">C &amp; G Trophy</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_cricket" title="County cricket">English domestic cricket</a> in the early part of the <a href="/wiki/2006_English_cricket_season" title="2006 English cricket season">2006 English cricket season</a>. They performed better than expected, winning three of their nine games, and finishing eighth in the Northern conference.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_e_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_e-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June, they played their first ODI since the <a href="/wiki/1999_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1999 Cricket World Cup">1999 World Cup</a> when they took on <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team" title="Pakistan national cricket team">Pakistan</a> in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-ODIList_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODIList-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Without key players Dougie Brown and <a href="/wiki/Navdeep_Poonia" title="Navdeep Poonia">Navdeep Poonia</a>, they lost by five wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_f_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_f-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> They finally got their first ODI win in the <a href="/wiki/European_Cricket_Championship" title="European Cricket Championship">European Championships</a> in August with a win over <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_cricket_team" title="Netherlands national cricket team">Holland</a> in a rain-shortened game.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_g_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_g-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> They again missed key players for some games in this tournament though, and thanks to their loss against Ireland, finished second in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-EC06_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC06-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 2006 and early 2007, Scotland participated in the third edition of the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2006\xe2\x80\x9307 ICC Intercontinental Cup">Intercontinental Cup</a>. They beat <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_cricket_team" title="Namibia national cricket team">Namibia</a> by an innings in May 2006, but draws against Ireland in August and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_cricket_team" title="United Arab Emirates national cricket team">United Arab Emirates</a> in January 2007 meant that they failed to reach the final.<sup id="cite_ref-ICCup06_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICCup06-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, they travelled to Test nation <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> for a two-match ODI series \xe2\x80\x93 their first outside the UK \xe2\x80\x93 but lost both matches heavily.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 2007, after the Intercontinental Cup match against United Arab Emirates in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah (city)">Sharjah</a>, they travelled to <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, first playing in a <a href="/wiki/Associates_Triangular_Series_in_Kenya_in_2006-07" class="mw-redirect" title="Associates Triangular Series in Kenya in 2006-07">tri-series</a> against <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_cricket_team" title="Canada national cricket team">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_cricket_team" title="Kenya national cricket team">Kenya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, which they finished second in.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_h_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_h-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This was followed by <a href="/wiki/2007_ICC_World_Cricket_League_Division_One" title="2007 ICC World Cricket League Division One">Division One</a> of the <a href="/wiki/World_Cricket_League" title="World Cricket League">World Cricket League</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, where Scotland finished as runners up.<sup id="cite_ref-WCL107_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCL107-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>They then travelled to <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> for their second <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">World Cup</a>. They again lost all their games and failed to progress beyond the first round.<sup id="cite_ref-WC07_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WC07-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Back in the UK, they competed in the <a href="/wiki/Friends_Provident_Trophy" title="Friends Provident Trophy">Friends Provident Trophy</a>, their only win coming against Lancashire.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_i_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_i-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> They also drew an Intercontinental Cup match against United Arab Emirates<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_j_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_j-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and an ODI against Pakistan in July was washed out.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_k_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_k-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July, Scotland took part in a <a href="/wiki/Quadrangular_Series_in_Ireland_in_2007" title="Quadrangular Series in Ireland in 2007">quadrangular series</a> in Ireland against the hosts, Holland and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a>. However, the endeavour was not a success. They lost their matches against Ireland and West Indies with the match against Holland being abandoned due to rain.\n</p><p>At the beginning of August, Scotland were on Intercontinental Cup duty as they won against Holland by an innings and 59 runs. They then drew with Ireland in a rain affected match, only gaining 3 points however after a poor 1st innings display. <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a> were Scotland\'s next ODI opponents in mid-August, which was shown live on BBC Scotland from Titwood, Glasgow. The match was reduced slightly to 46 overs after a couple of brief showers, but India won by 7 wickets.\n</p><p>Having reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/World_Cricket_League" title="World Cricket League">World Cricket League</a> earlier in the year, Scotland qualified to play in the <a href="/wiki/2007_Twenty20_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Twenty20 World Championship">Twenty20 World Championship</a> held in South Africa. They lost by 51 runs to Pakistan in their first game, and did not get a chance to play their other Group D opponents <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a>, as the game was washed out without a ball being bowled.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In July 2008, Scotland played a <a href="/wiki/2008_Associates_Tri-Series_in_Scotland" title="2008 Associates Tri-Series in Scotland">tri-series</a> against New Zealand and Ireland in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, Scotland. Scotland beat Ireland but lost their match against New Zealand.\n</p><p>In early August, Scotland participated with five other Associate nations in the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20_Qualifier" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier">2009 ICC World Twenty20 Qualifier</a> in Belfast. Despite an initial loss to hosts Ireland, victory against Bermuda secured a semi final slot. Throwing off the disappointment of an unexpected loss to Holland in the semi-final a few hours earlier, Scotland bounced right back for a 9 wicket victory over Kenya (who had advanced ahead of Canada), to secure third place. However, with only two nations guaranteed to progress, qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009 ICC World Twenty20</a> was only granted when Zimbabwe confirmed that they would not attend the tournament.\n</p><p>On 18 August, Scotland played their first ODI encounter against England. Hosting the Auld Enemy, at the Grange Cricket Club in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. However the match was abandoned due to rain after less than 3 overs of England\'s reply to Scotland\'s 156/9.\n</p><p>In December 2008, <a href="/wiki/Cricket_Scotland" title="Cricket Scotland">Cricket Scotland</a>, the governing body of Scottish cricket, took the historic act of giving three Scotland players central contracts. Bowlers <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Goudie" title="Gordon Goudie">Gordon Goudie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dewald_Nel" title="Dewald Nel">Dewald Nel</a> and captain <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Watson_(cricketer)" title="Ryan Watson (cricketer)">Ryan Watson</a> became the first full-time professional cricketers based in Scotland. Nineteen other cricketers have been offered part-time professional deals.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2008_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scotland participated in the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2009 ICC World Twenty20">2009 ICC World Twenty20</a> in England in June 2009. They were drawn alongside Test nations <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_cricket_team" title="New Zealand national cricket team">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team" title="South Africa national cricket team">South Africa</a> in Group D, with both matches being played at <a href="/wiki/The_Oval" title="The Oval">The Oval</a> in London.\n</p><p>The first match, against New Zealand, was shortened to 7 overs per side due to rain. Scotland batted first and made 89/4, with <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Coetzer" title="Kyle Coetzer">Kyle Coetzer</a> top-scoring with 33. However, three no-balls and a dropped catch enabled New Zealand to win by seven wickets with an over to spare.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2009_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2009-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the second match, South Africa made 211/5, with <a href="/wiki/AB_de_Villiers" title="AB de Villiers">AB de Villiers</a> hitting 79 not out off only 34 balls. In response, Scotland were bowled out for 81, more than half of which was scored by Coetzer (42). The 130-run margin of defeat was the second-largest in terms of runs in a Twenty20 International.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2009a_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2009a-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2010, Scotland took part in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/ECB_40" title="ECB 40">ECB 40</a> tournament.\n</p><p>Scotland competed in the qualifiers in the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, to compete for a place in the <a href="/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2010 ICC World Twenty20">2010 ICC World Twenty20</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">West Indies</a>. They competed for a place with <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_cricket_team" title="Afghanistan national cricket team">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_national_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian national cricket team">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland national cricket team">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_cricket_team" title="Kenya national cricket team">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_cricket_team" title="Netherlands national cricket team">Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_cricket_team" title="United Arab Emirates national cricket team">United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_cricket_team" title="United States national cricket team">USA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_l_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_l-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The tournament was disappointing for Scotland, going out in the group stage without winning a single match.\n</p><p>Scotland\xe2\x80\x99s Intercontinental Cup campaign was more successful as they reached the final in December - against Afghanistan - at the bespoke new cricket stadium in Dubai. Scheduled as a four-day first-class match of two innings each side, Afghanistan won the game in eight sessions. This was also the first cricket match of any kind that was live-streamed online - by two Scottish fans, with the agreement of the ICC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICC_World_Cup_Qualifiers">ICC World Cup Qualifiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: ICC World Cup Qualifiers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During March and April 2009 Scotland attempted to defend the ICC Trophy they won in 2005. To secure qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2011 Cricket World Cup">2011 Cricket World Cup</a> a top four place was targeted. They were also attempting to secure ODI status by finishing in the top six.\n</p><p>Scotland started the tournament badly by losing three of their five group games. With only the points earned against Namibia being taken through to the Super Eights, Scotland faced a difficult route to the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2009b_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2009b-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland started the Super Eights well by beating Holland in their first match. Defeats against Kenya and Afghanistan followed. The result of which threatened Scotland\'s qualification for the World Cup as well as the possibility of losing their ODI status if they finished out of the top six.\n</p><p>Victory against United Arab Emirates in their last game, and an improved run-rate, thanks to the 122 run victory, ensured a top six place for the Scots, securing ODI status until the next round of World Cup qualifiers.\n</p><p>The Scottish team qualified for the ICC <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Cricket World Cup 2015">Cricket World Cup 2015</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, but was eliminated after six straight losses out of six matches.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand_A_tour_of_Scotland_in_2014">New Zealand A tour of Scotland in 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: New Zealand A tour of Scotland in 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In August 2014, Scotland played a three match series against <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_A_cricket_team" title="New Zealand A cricket team">New Zealand A</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cambusdoon_New_Ground" title="Cambusdoon New Ground">Cambusdoon New Ground</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayr" title="Ayr">Ayr</a>. In the first match <a href="/wiki/Grant_Elliott" title="Grant Elliott">Grant Elliott</a> and captain <a href="/wiki/BJ_Watling" title="BJ Watling">BJ Watling</a> scored centuries and ensured that New Zealand A won by 199 runs. Scotland conceded nearly 150 runs in the last ten overs.\n</p><p>In January 2017 Scotland took part in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Desert_T20_Challenge" title="2017 Desert T20 Challenge">2017 Desert T20 Challenge</a>. They won all three of their group fixtures, before losing to <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland national cricket team">Ireland</a> in the semi-finals.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe_tour_of_Scotland_in_2017">Zimbabwe tour of Scotland in 2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scotland_national_cricket_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe tour of Scotland in 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Scotland achieved their first victory against a <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">full member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">ICC</a> when it defeated a <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_cricket_team_in_Scotland_in_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwe cricket team in Scotland in 2017">touring</a> <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_cricket_team" title="Zimbabwe national cricket team">Zimbabwe</a> side.\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table style="float:left; width:15%; table-layout:fixed; border-style:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td href="/wiki/England_national_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="England national cricket team">England</a> side.\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<div style="width: 100%; clear:both">\n<table three consecutive ODIs.<sup id="cite_ref-Stats_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stats-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></i></li></ul></div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
